40~The system shall provide adequate capability to allow the operator to operate each UAV within its certified operational flight envelope.
8~Appropriate cautions and warnings shall be provided to the operator if the air vehicle deviates into unsafe flight regime.
194~For mission planning, the system shall provide terrain avoidance warning and minimum reception altitude calculations for line of sight flights.
2~During mission execution, the system shall provide the operator a cautions and warnings when the UAV system has identified a malfunction.
5848~The system shall provide the required information to allow the operator to maintain safe separation from other aircraft and a safe altitude in civilian airspace per Federal Aviation Administration (FAA) rules.
352~The system shall be designed such that no single hardware failure results in an unsafe command to be transmitted to the air vehicle.
352~The system shall be designed such that no single software error results in an unsafe command to be transmitted to the air vehicle.
88~The system shall be capable of restoring power in sufficient time to avoid loss of air vehicle control during power outages.
12~The system shall monitor the uplink and downlink to each UAV under its control.
4~Upon detection of loss of link, the system shall attempt to reestablish communications with the air vehicle.
10~The system design shall provide protection against injury to system operators and maintenance personnel..
23596~The system design shall use MIL STD 2036, Section 5.1.3.11 as a guide, with regard to personnel hazards, and MIL STD 1472D, Section 5.13, as a guide for safety from a human engineering viewpoint.
11~System safety and health hazards, if any, shall be identified and evaluated during Phase I of the system development.
94~Risk levels and a program to manage the probability and severity of hazards shall also be developed.
1~The system is an Automated Information System (AIS).
17868~Therefore, as per DoD Regulation 5000.2 R, dated March 15, 1996, the system shall meet security requirements in accordance with DoD Directive 5200.28(D), "Security Requirements for Automated Information Systems" dated March 21, 1988.
2528~The system shall be accredited by the Designated Approving Authority prior to processing classified as well as sensitive unclassified data.
7720~Using risk assessment procedures defined in DoD 5200.28(D), a risk index and the minimum security requirements for system shall be determined.
5892~The inputs to this procedure are the clearance or authorization of the system users and the sensitivities of the data that the system processes, stores or transfers.
2~These requirements pertain to the system computer hardware and software.
7152~The system data sensitivities shall be determined by the data sensitivities of the systems with which it interfaces, to including the air vehicles, payloads, and C4I systems.
38990~Links that provide communications between the system and other systems shall be secured in a manner appropriate for the sensitivities of the material passed through such links, in accordance with DoD Directive C 5200.5, "Communication Security (COMSEC)" dated 21 April 1990.
24~The system shall be designed to protect its communication and data links against enemy Electronic Warfare (EW) threats, physical anti radiation weaponry and physical destruction.
286212~All hardware, software, documentation, and sensitive information processed by system shall be physically protected, minimally at the level determined by the risk index computed in Section 3.8.1, to prevent intentional as well as unintentional disclosure, destruction, and modification.
271~The system shall be approved for operation at the same level as the systems with which it interfaces.
84288~All system users, operators, maintainers and other personnel having access to system shall be cleared to the highest sensitivity of the data that the system processes, stores and transfers.
16~Additional local site procedures shall be developed to prevent the intentional or unintentional disclosure of sensitive information to unauthorized individuals.
300~A training program consisting of an initial security training and awareness briefing covering AIS security in general but also tailored to the system shall be developed.
1936~The system shall be capable of operation within environments specified in the System or Subsystem Design Document for the land based shelter and shipboard environments.
4~The system hardware shall be mounted as well as ruggedized to withstand inter and intra theater movement.
50460~The system hardware will provide the functionality and capability to receive, process, and disseminate video and telemetry data from the AV and payload perform mission planning monitor and control the payload monitor and control the AV and monitor and control the data links.
456~The hardware of the system shall be capable of being scaled as well as being modular to meet the varying needs of the Services.
135908~The system hardware shall allow for long range communications from one system to another, data storage expansion, access to other computers to share in processing capability, and multiple external peripherals.
60~The system hardware shall support the data rate characteristics of the AV, data link and payload to ensure interoperability.
2~For each OUTRIDER system, the system shall provide full independent computer redundancy.
60~The system shall conform with the National Institute for Standard Technology (NIST) Federal Information Processing Standard (FIPS) Publication 151 2 (POSIX.1).
12~The system shall have sufficient throughput to support the processing requirements of the selected data link.
48~To meet growth requirements, the system shall be capable of adding additional storage without major hardware reconfiguration.
75228~The system computer system shall contain a CD ROM drive that is compatible with National Imagery and Mapping Agency (NIMA), CD ROM Digital Terrain Elevation Data (DTED), Digital Feature Analysis Data (DFAD), and embedded training media.
24~The system shall use standard military worldwide 110 or 220 volt 50 or 60 hertz generators and commercial power sources.
372~The system shall use standard electrical power sources available within the DoD family of ground mobile, airborne, and shipboard electrical power sources.
2462~The system shall be capable of restoring power in sufficient time to avoid loss of critical mission data and loss of air vehicle control during power outages.
280~The system shall have an uninterrupted power supply for critical phases (landing and takeoff as a minimum) of mission execution.
95424~The system throughput shall not exceed 50% of the throughput capability delivered over any 10 second period, and as an objective throughput shall not exceed 25% of throughput capability delivered over any 10 second period.
33~The system shall be capable of providing a 50% spare memory storage capacity over delivered storage used.
17~As an objective a 75% spare memory storage capacity over storage used shall be provided.
50460~The system software will provide the functionality and capability to receive, process, and disseminate video and telemetry data from the AV and payload perform mission planning monitor and control the payload monitor and control the AV and monitor and control the data links.
2515~The system shall have software based on Defense Information Infrastructure or Common Operating Environment per Assistant Secretary of Defense for Command, Control, Communications, and Intelligence (ASD(C3I)) Joint Technical Architecture (JTA).
26~The system shall comply with the Assistant Secretary of Defense (C3I) Joint Technical Architecture (JTA).
95~This includes, but is not limited to, the language, the computer, database, architecture, and interoperability.
34832~The system shall provide an open software architecture to be capable of supporting additional CSCIs, CSCs, and CSUs for future AVs, future payloads, and payload capabilities (for example auto search and automatic target tracking), and future Tactical UAVs.
4548~The system core software shall be generically written to provide level one through level five interaction for both Outrider and Predator UAVs and establish the architecture for future tactical UAVs.
1904~The system software shall provide the UAV operator with the necessary tools for computer related communications, mission tasking, mission planning, mission execution, data receipt, data processing, and data dissemination.
158~The system software shall be capable of being hosted on a variety of computer operating systems that are organic to the various Services.
1~system software shall provide a windows based graphic operator interface.
2~The system software shall be non proprietary and have unlimited data rights.
82~The system's operating system and executable software shall be re programmable without hardware disassembly.
12~Training software shall be alterable without affecting the configuration of the operational software.
180~Training software is the software that provides the computer based training functionality for the system operator.
82~The system software shall restrict the operator(s) from exercising levels of interaction not achievable by the system.
11220~The system software shall provide a high resolution, computer generated, graphical user interface that enables the UAV operator that is trained on one system to control different types of UAVs as well as UAV payloads with minimal additional training.
30584~Each control console shall have, at a minimum, the capability to display the following four display windows: display to provide aircraft position, system position, flight path, and a waypoint graphics in the foreground which are positioned in relation to a map displayed in the background.
16~A display to provide graphic presentations of downlinked telemetry data, and display to present the interface menus for workstation software.
157~The DII or COE UCP or CMP shall provide a consistent and common set of interfaces for United States Message Text Format (USMTF), Army Tactical Command Control System (AsystemS), and Field Artillery Tactical Data Systems (FATDS) message sets.
4~The TACCOM segment shall provide external interfaces for the communications media.
18432~The TACCOM segment shall provide API's for the transmission of imagery in National Imagery Transmission Formats 1.1a and 2.0 as per MILSTD 2500 and to be compatible with the Common Imagery Ground or Surface Station (CGIS) Guidelines.
6751~The system data latency shall not be greater than that present in the Predator ground control station or Outrider ground control station, whichever is smaller.
2496~The system reliability will be considered in every phase of the design and development process and shall achieve a system reliability (Mean Time Between Failures MTBF) equal to or greater than that which is specified in the Predator and Outrider ORDs.
33376~The system maintainability will be considered in every phase of the design and development process and shall achieve a system maintainability (Mean Time To Repair MTTR) equal to or greater than that which is specified in the Predator and Outrider ORDs.
2214~The system equipment shall achieve an availability (Ao), as defined below, equal to or greater than that which is specified in the Predator and Outrider ORDs.
23856~The total, fully useable, addressable, physically present program instruction memory and data storage memory for each processor shall have at least 50% unused memory during the Normal Operations Mode over any 10 second period.
26211014~The processing speed of each processor shall be such that at least 50% of the throughput of each processor remains unused over all 10 second periods and at least 20% of the throughput of each processor remains unused over one second periods regardless of the system function performed.
1814~The I or O channel reserve capability for each processor shall have at least a 50% reserve, addressable and useable, I or O channel capacity over any 10 second period.
168~system software flexibility and expandability shall be provided through use of the DII COE and through use of standardized software development practices.
358~Hardware and software shall be selected for use in the system with the goal of providing ease of future changes to the system elements.
49592~The object of portability for the system is to select or develop hardware which will readily host emerging software packages and software which will be as independent of host hardware as possible.
7560~The selection of processors, interface cards for communication interfaces, disk drives, video, networking equipment, and all other hardware for use in the system shall be made according to standards for production of an open architecture.
114~The selection of operating system and programming language for use in the system shall be made according to standards for development of an open architecture.
4~Testability shall be considered in the design and development of the system.
1~The system shall be functionally and physically partitioned to allow for efficient fault isolation.
14~Control over internal items and devices shall be provided for detecting and isolating internal faults.
106~Test points and data paths shall be defined to support efficient fault isolation.
97~The system shall provide the common software architecture for system interaction with Predator, Outrider, and future Tactical UAVs.
232~In the selection of hardware design solutions to satisfy the requirements herein, Non Developmental Items (NDI) (off the shelf equipment previously approved for service use) shall be chosen to the maximum practicable extent.
4~If NDI that provides the desired functions can not be identified, then Commercial Off The Shelf (COTS) hardware may be used.
228~During Phase 1, design and construction will be accomplished in accordance with commercial best practices unless otherwise required to meet a specific service operational environmental factor.
3768~Design and construction requirements for Phase 2 will be revised to reflect appropriate government approved sub tier specifications controlling all aspects of electrical and electronic or mechanical designs for new or modified system equipment.
3~System documentation shall be developed as part of the system program and will follow MIL STD 498 for format.
6~The documentation developed shall contain sufficient level of detail to identify the functional, operational and design requirements of the system.
38~The documentation shall contain sufficient technical detail to define the hardware and software design implemented to satisfy the system requirements.
4005~system material factors shall be governed by the NDI, GFE and COTS specifications developed by the equipment manufacturers, where applicable.
75~During Phase 1, control techniques to minimize electromagnetic interference, emanation, and susceptibility shall be used in the design of system equipment.
173~This control will be inherent in the design of the system and the electrical and electronic equipment components and assemblies thereof.
84~The susceptibility to coupling and the propagation of Electromagnetic Interference (EMI) will be minimized by component location, cable routing, and judicious use of shielding.
109132~There shall be neither unacceptable response nor malfunction of any system and associated equipment due to EMI produced by any as well as all of the system and equipment associated with the system.
78~The system shall be compatible with the external electromagnetic environment that is typical of the service specific environment in the system will be operated.
5~The specific electromagnetic environment values will be determined during Phase I of the system development.
27~The system design shall ensure that personnel, fuel, and ordinance are not exposed to electromagnetic radiation as a result of operating the system.
29~The specific radiation hazard (RADHAZ) and HERO values will be determined during Phase I of the system development.
59~As system transitions into Phase 2, electromagnetic radiation safety and operation specifications will be invoked in the LRIP specification.
2~Newly designed software shall be developed in accordance with a tailored MIL STD 498.
176~Software written for other systems shall be used in system where it is determined that the existing software is suitable for use within the system software.
11385~A modular architecture shall be used by the system software in order to support future interoperability with multiple types of UAVs and payloads while maintaining consistent displays and user interfaces.
444~Software components satisfying common planning and control functions will allow for vehicle specific components to be integrated in the future.
1456~system hardware flexibility and expansion shall be provided through use of GFE, NDI and COTS hardware designed to be upgraded and expanded.
18~After emplacement at the operational site, the system shall be capable of planning and launching a mission within 1 hour of tasking.
111465~Required activities include 1) mission planning of a minimum 1 waypoint mission, 2) preparing 2 AVs for flight, 3) data terminal set up, 4) safety equipment emplaced, 5) and a single AV launched.
7~The system shall be capable of operating continuously in functional Operation Mode for a minimum of 72 hours.
3619~The system shall have ergonomically designed operator controls and displays for the 5th percentile female to 95th percentile male operator.
52~The controls shall allow the air vehicle and payload operators to perform mission control, mission monitoring, and mission updates and modifications while wearing cold weather clothing and in a Mission Oriented Protective Posture.
190~The system shall provide the operator a caution and warning diagnostic when the system has identified a malfunction.
266~The system shall have monitor(s) that allow reading of displays under direct sunlight and low light level environments.
1~The system HCI shall be a Graphical User Interface (GUI) based on X windows and Motif.
36~When performing a given task during mission execution, the operator shall be given appropriate warning messages from other concurrently executing subsystem tasks.
3~system Warning messages shall be color coded and flashed based on mission criticality.
10~The color codes and flash frequencies will follow MIL STD 1472 guidelines.
80062~The system operator shall be required to enter an acknowledgment prior to disabling the display of critical warning flags for any AV, Payload, ADT, GDT, and system faults.
9~A combination of visual and auditory outputs will be provided to alert the system operator to situations which may require operator response.
16200~Visual alerts to the system operator shall be in the form of a displayed message box that has a display priority greater than other existing windows to ensure that it is viewable immediately by the operator..
18~The position of the displayed message window shall be easily adjustable by the operator to ensure that important mission data is not obscured.
44~In addition to displayed alert messages to the system operator, auditory alerts to include tones shall also be provided.
1541~The volume of these auditory tones shall be adjustable by the operator via keyboard and trackball input to at least 20dB above the speech interference level at the operator's ear.
10~All system warning messages and HCI actions shall be archived for later review.
1579~All system operator inputs shall be error checked such that any erroneous operator entry will not cause current processing to terminate.
4~The HCI shall prompt the operator for a valid input.
2~Display jitter and flicker shall not be perceptible by the operator.
30~The operational tasks to be performed concurrently by the operator during normal operation will be determined by appropriate task analysis and function allocation.
16~The system shall facilitate Human Computer Interfaces (HCIs) that support operation of all system modes, functions, and capabilities.
26~The Human Computer Interface (HCI) shall be designed and implemented in accordance with the system HCI Specification.
4~The HCI shall provide redundancy in all operations, so that the loss of any one HCI input device does not prohibit operation of any system function.
139~The system shall provide the functionality to display all HCI elements on any available monitor on the system workstation.
12365~The system shall be capable of displaying a window within a window format to include, as a minimum, displaying a video window overlaid on a map screen as well as a map screen overlaid on a video screen.
1581~The system shall provide full complementary control operations from the keyset as well as the X or Y control device (e.g, trackball, mouse, joystick).
16~The system shall provide access to the DII Style Manager so that pointing device characteristics can be modified.
56560~The system shall provide the functionality to have a maximum delay time of 1 second from operator command to system acknowledgement and response.[SSS 559] The system shall provide a capability for porting an off the shelf, complex control joystick with multiple toggle and multi position switches as part of the system hardware suite.
94~The system shall use graphical representations to convey information, such as system status, C4I links, and AV GDT links.
18~The system shall provide for multi level information display tailoring by the operator.
115~The system shall provide automated system information, control options, and logical and simple operator guidance and support for immediate and adaptive responding to crisis situations.
1440~The system shall provide maximum automated system software support to system status monitoring and alerting of the system operator when a preset system parameter goes under as well as over a set threshold.
62~The system shall provide the necessary processing, display, and control capabilities to ensure dynamic situational awareness input to the system operator.
22~The system shall minimize alphanumeric data display in favor of graphic, pictorial information display.
1196~The system HCI shall provide unambiguous AV and payload control and status feedback indicators to ensure safe, efficient operations of two AVs and their payloads by a single system station.
19200~The system shall provide for a specific icon shape on a constant contrast background, as well as other visual information coding mechanisms, to cue the system operator regarding which UAVs are under his or her primary control.
21~The system HCI shall provide the capability to select and amplify an object and point on a map as well as payload screen.
3~The system HCI shall provide coarse and fine payload control capabilities directly on the payload screen.
2~The system HCI shall display the SAR imaging swath on the map display.
41~The system HCI shall provide the on screen capability to select and efficiently move as well as reorient a previously defined SAR imaging swath.
9~The system HCI shall provide the capability to lock onto and hold a coordinate point on the payload imagery window.
2997~The system HCI shall provide the capability to display operator definable "Lock Out" zones around waypoints, Launch and Recovery Point (LRP), as well as any selected point on the AV flight path.
4~The system HCI shall provide for a rapid means to cancel aural warnings.
132~The system HCI shall provide for separation, grouping, and visual coding of multiple categories of alerts, to include Warnings, Cautions, and Advisories.
2844~The system HCI shall provide for visual Warnings, Cautions, and Advisories to be displayed at or near the center of the field of view, i.e, within a 30o cone, of all monitors in a system.
63120~For AV safety as well as mission critical Warnings, the system HCI shall provide a default selection as well as an override option, along with a selection of adaptive responses, and the minimum information necessary to assist the operator in responding quickly and adaptively to the emergency.
11944~The system HCI shall provide for on screen information to include, as a minimum, overlays, headers, cursors, alphanumeric annotation, waypoints, crosshairs, designed to be visible against the complete spectrum of map and payload video backgrounds.
60~The system HCI shall provide continuously available, on screen control functions for time and missioncritical operations, to include as a minimum print, freeze, declassification, mark VCR, declutter, cease RF transmission.
28~The system HCI shall provide for the capability to automatically designate target locations from the payload screen onto the map screen.

639755~To the maximum extent possible, general purpose test equipment (GPTE) and common tools resident in each service shall be used to perform all corrective and preventative maintenance at all authorized levels of maintenance.
97552~Tools and test equipment required to maintain the system but not resident in each service inventory shall be identified as special tools and special purpose test equipment (SPTE), respectively, and kept to a minimum.

2916~System Architecture: Broad system level needs, such as flexible configuration, should be addressed by systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT.
1403424~Data Requirements: Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT need a variety of data to support investigations, including data regarding demographics, cases, exposures, investigations, agents, contacts, specimen or sample collection, laboratory tests, travel and conveyance, and restriction monitoring.
350~System Functions and Behaviors: Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should support case investigation, maintain detailed and comprehensive linkages, trace contacts, and quarantine and isolation monitoring activities.
46120~Analysis, Visualization, and Report Generation: Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should enable investigators to produce both aggregated and individual reports about affected entities and events.
19458~System Integration and Data Exchange: OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT information must be exchangeable, based on established standards, between systems involved in the investigation, identification, confirmation, and reporting of a health event.
88~Vocabulary Standards: Standard vocabulary lists and data structures have been defined by standards organizations.
1~Where they exist, systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should use them.
2~As additional standards are defined, they should be accepted and implemented
5708~Operations: Personnel, roles, activities, and responsibilities necessary to support all aspects of OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be clearly defined.
11424~System Security and Availability: Security of OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT data includes the protection of data from corruption and access by unauthorized individuals, as well as the protection of the actual systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT from sabotage or other failure.
4~A plan must be established for continuing activities when systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT are unavailable.
4~Privacy: Patients, organizations, and personnel must be protected from fraudulent and unauthorized use of their information.
33970~Systems designed to support OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must offer configuration flexibility so that new data fields, entities, entity types and relationship types may be added to capture information unique to each particular health event.
2240~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must support structured data entry for common forms and fields to ensure data integrity, validity, and standardization.
32~A standardized data structure ensures that data mapping of common elements will only be necessary one time, rather than for each event.
2~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should support multiple deployment options.
5968~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should provide the ability for computers in disconnected mode to reconnect to a server to share OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT data among other computers that operate in disconnected mode.
7392~OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT data should be synchronized so that all instances of OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT applications working from the same server are able to share and use the same data.
4732~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to electronically record and store data from remote devices that may be uploaded to an aggregating system.
3~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be capable of using configurable, domain specific vocabulary.
7482~The following high level data requirements are necessary to ensure that the data being collected, analyzed, and reported to support OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT are clearly defined.
12~An entity is any being or object involved in a health event.
2~Entities may be classified as a person, organization, location, animal, object, conveyance, event, or other organism.
12~Each type of entity requires specific data to be collected.
7560~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture demographic data about persons involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: Subject ID, name, address, date of birth, gender, phone number, race, ethnicity, and country of citizenship.
1~Other descriptive details may be captured, such as occupation and work history.
1012~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about organizations involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: organization name, location, and contact information.
1376~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about locations involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: name, type, street address, city, state, zip code, country, GPS coordinates, and other specific details.
197200~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about any animals involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: type, age, gender, owner's name and address, color, weight, and species.
8~A Subject ID should also be collected for animals in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation.
8~It may be a challenge to ensure unambiguous identification because demographic details of an animal are not easily identified therefore, animals involved in investigations may need to be tagged.
563584~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data for any object involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, such as a letter, invoice, food item, or any object that cannot be classified as a "person, organization, place, or animal.".
104~Collected data may include: name of the object, type, physical descriptors, address, identification number, and relevant dates and times.
39700~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about any conveyance involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: type of conveyance, route taken, etc.
3070604~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about any public or private gathering of people involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: time, location, nature of the event, etc.
88512~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture data about any living things other than persons or animals that are involved in an OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigation, including: type of living thing, and other customizable data collection questions.
290~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the capability to capture an entity's travel history to support investigations of entities infected, exposed or potentially exposed.
72~When a health event is investigated, it must be assigned an event identifier that is unique within the jurisdiction.
48~Data describing the health event should be captured, including the reason for the investigation, the category of event, the date the event began, the suspected agent or investigation focus, the geographic area impacted by the event, as well as the event status.
11~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to record the case definition for a health event.
14~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to capture changes to the case definition that occur as the health event evolves.
56~Travel history provides specific information to indicate when, where, and how subjects involved in an event traveled to a location, and conveyance data describes the vehicle in which the travel occurred.
12878~Examples of travel history include a person's local travel as a part of their daily activities as well as the shipment of animals or plants from one country to another.
5602~Travel history data should include information such as the method of transportation, flight number, departure and arrival dates and times, and the origination and destination locations.
5~Information about each leg of a trip, as well as the parent information about the trip, should be captured.
7140~For example, if a person who lives in Georgia travels to Seattle and becomes exposed to monkey pox, then visits a friend in Santa Fe, travel history and conveyance data should be noted accordingly for each place the exposed person traveled.
2240~Travel history data to be collected for an animal or object should include shipping invoices, animal shelter delivery and adoption receipts, and delivery schedules.
26728~Detailed conveyance data must be collected when relevant to the investigation, including the carrier identifier, the type of conveyance, as well as the make, model, year, and identification number of each vehicle with which the entity was in contact.
12~Case and exposure data provide more detailed information beyond demographic data.
1971~Cases can be persons or animals, and exposure contacts can be persons, animals, other organisms, or exposure settings, such as travel conveyance, location, organization, object, or event.
270~Because attributes of both case and exposure data may describe the same entity, systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the ability to avoid capturing redundant entity demographic information.
15360~Case data about the entity should include: a case identifier that is unique within the jurisdiction being reported, the suspected agent, case diagnosis, health status, case status, investigation dates, clinical history, symptom onset date and time, epidemiological links to other cases, and priority.
48~There must be a means to update the case diagnosis either manually or automatically if the case definition changes during an event.
12~Epidemiological data must be collected to assist in the case investigation of events.
29888~Standard Epidemiological data to be collected includes: onset date and time of symptoms, type of symptoms, risk factors, medical history data, laboratory data, procedure data, and questionnaire responses.
30~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must allow for dynamic, event specific case investigation data to be captured.
12~In the context of a case, all entities exposed to a case must be recorded and linked to the case.
228~Demographic information should be collected about the investigator, including their name, address, and contact information, so that the investigator may be contacted to answer questions or to provide additional information.
36~Both the jurisdiction investigating the event and the jurisdiction reporting the cases and associated investigations must be captured.
1136~For example, if a person becomes ill during travel in one jurisdiction but is the resident of another, the illness will be reported by the state of residence and investigated by the jurisdiction visited.
83~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to classify entities associated with the investigation as investigation controls.
20~For example, controls share demographic characteristics with the subject of the case, but are not infected with the agent that is the focus of the investigation.
8028~Exposure investigation data to be captured must include information related to exposure levels, type of exposure, place of exposure, length of time the entity was exposed, frequency of exposure, and the entity's proximity to the source of exposure.
192~Detailed data must be collected about the source of exposure as well as the exposed entity to support contact exposure tracing.
1037792~Exposure data related to both the potential source and the potential spread include the entity's type, Subject ID, Contact ID, contact's name and address, exposure dates and times, health status, and priority code.
16~Epidemiological data must be collected to assist in the exposure investigation of health events.
11456~Standard Epidemiological data to be collected for exposure investigation parallels the data to be collected for case investigation and includes: onset date and time of symptoms, type of symptoms, risk factors, laboratory data, procedure data, and questionnaire responses.
79~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must support capturing dynamic, event specific data that describes contact between two subjects.
13376~Monitoring and follow up data is used to track the progress and treatment of subjects who were exposed or potentially exposed to a health event.
3534~For more information about monitoring and follow up data, please reference "PHIN Countermeasure or Response Administration Functional Requirements and Process Flows", available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
91~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should support the monitoring and follow up activities required when tracking the status of cases and exposed individuals.
1504~Monitoring data should be collected about cases and exposed individuals who are isolated or quarantined because of a health event.
14660~Follow up data should be collected from subjects or their proxies to track symptoms and compliance with recommended treatment plans or prophylaxis.
36~Follow up data may be received from take response exams of persons who received a countermeasure that requires such an exam.
38852~Specimen or sample collection and laboratory response data supports the collection of clinical specimens, food samples, environmental samples, and other types of samples that will be tested for biological, chemical, and radiological agents.
20576~These specimens or samples can be collected from places, persons, animals, or environmental sources such as air, water, food, or soil.
144~Specimens or samples collected for laboratory testing must be assigned an identifier that is unique within the jurisdiction.
13408~The subject of a specimen or sample collected for laboratory testing must be linked to the specimen or sample by an identifier that is unique within the jurisdiction.
5528~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to store data about the specimens or samples that are collected for laboratory testing.
7952~Examples of this data are: Specimen ID, Subject ID, purpose for test, collection date and time, subject type, specimen category, specimen type, suspected agent, risk indicator, person performing specimen or sample collection, location of collection, and volume and quantity details.
68~Clinical specimen data should include information about the specimen source or site from which the specimen was taken, symptom date of onset, and whether the sample is acute or convalescent.
14176~Environmental sample data should include information about the collection method, location from which the sample was taken, source, nature of the sample, quality control data, collection begin and end date and time for air samples, and original volume and volume of concentrate tested for water samples.
12~Food sample data should include information about the lot number, batch number, manufacturer name, shipping invoice, temperature, sample type, and product storage condition.
24~Bar coding should be supported for the capture of detailed specimen or sample data to improve the quality and efficiency of data collection.
22~Chain of custody information for all specimens or samples should be captured.
5280~Chain of custody information for forensic and select agent samples must be captured, including the person who collected the sample, the location of collection, all people who came into contact with the sample during the preparation for shipment to the laboratory, and the acceptance of the package by the shipper.
274~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to create a laboratory test request for a specimen or sample or group of specimens or samples.
34~More information about creating laboratory test requests is found in section 2.5 System Integration and Data Exchange of this document.
35940~Information about batch shipments of specimens or samples that are transferred to test laboratories or other facilities must be collected, including the shipper, shipment tracking number, and the sending organization's contact information.
155162~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to support the inclusion of labeling, packaging and shipping instructions, and the shipping manifest with batch shipments of specimens or samples.
86~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to store laboratory results and link the results to the original laboratory test request.
282~More information about receiving and linking laboratory test requests is found in section 2.5 System Integration and Data Exchange of this document.
4~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must store data about laboratory results.
58176~Examples of this data include the Specimen ID, Subject ID, test date and time, test type, data for each organization involved in the testing of the specimen or sample, laboratory results and result values, other data such as unit of measure for result value, overall interpretation, and any relevant notes.
12~If the specimen or sample collection record exists, the laboratory result must be linked to the specimen collection record by the Specimen ID.
18~If the specimen or sample collection record does not exist, the laboratory result must be linked to the subject by the Subject ID.
2~All levels of granularity of results must be supported.
496800~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should capture or be linked to data regarding the prophylaxis or treatment to cases, exposed individuals, or at risk persons, including the person who ordered the prophylaxis or treatment, and the name, date, type, duration, and dosage of the treatment or prophylaxis given.
103106~For specific data requirements regarding the administration of prophylaxis and treatment, please reference PHIN Preparedness Countermeasure or Response Administration Functional Requirements and Process Flows, available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
32~Contraindication information should be collected to indicate why vaccinations, treatments, or antidotes may not have been administered or why the patient may not have complied with prescribed interventions.
662336~If an affected person suffers a negative reaction to a vaccine or prophylaxis that was administered, adverse event data may be collected and used to determine the need for additional interventions or to determine if there is a problem with the pharmaceutical, batch, or the administering facility or person.
39880~For specific data requirements regarding adverse event data, please reference PHIN Preparedness Countermeasure or Response Administration Functional Requirements and Process Flows, available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
51~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should capture information such as the date and time of an activity, activity type, who initiated the activity, and contact information to generate activity logs for management purposes.
6~Activity logs, which are tools for investigators to track their actions during a case, should be supported.
20~For example, investigators may log calls made to monitor symptoms or calls made to schedule follow up visits.
52~Activity logs may also provide information needed to support communication with various jurisdictions in the event that the investigation crosses jurisdictional boundaries.
142~For example, if a person becomes ill during travel in one jurisdiction but is the resident of another, the illness will be reported by the state of residence, rather than by the jurisdiction visited.
1~Electronic questionnaires must be developed and validated.
64~They will be designed by investigators to collect common data elements, agent specific data elements, and other customized data elements.
1~Electronic questionnaires should provide the capability to accept digital signatures.
6~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must provide the ability to control the configuration of and revisions to investigation specific questionnaires.
10~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must provide the ability to publish investigation specific questionnaires and implementation guides.
10~Case investigation should be supported by reusable questionnaire libraries that use common terminology to maximize the efficiency of data exchange.
556~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should provide a manual or automatic means of updating the status of case records as the case definition changes.
107~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should track the changes made to the status of case records as a result of changes in the case definition.
6~Linkages allow investigators to create meaningful analysis, characterize the event, and identify at risk populations.
144~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must support dynamically defined associations between entities for the purpose of defining relationships.
2~For example, person to person, person to place, animal to person, object to place, person to travel.
152472~Entity to Epidemiological data links must match the entity to their symptoms, survey questions, specimens or samples collected, laboratory results, and prophylaxis and treatment data.
4~Each new case must be able to link an assigned Entity ID to an Event ID within the scope of the investigation.
62728~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT require the ability to capture information about possible cases and potential contacts from the identification process through the treatment and follow up process, as supported by linkages among entities, events, and actions.
396~Laboratory results must be linked to corresponding specimens or samples including multiple results from one specimen or sample), and subjects when the participating laboratory returns the results.
19~These linkages must unambiguously associate multiple laboratory results to case and contact identifiers.
75~If the specimen or sample was created from another specimen or sample, laboratory results for the child specimens or samples must be linked to the corresponding parent specimen or sample.
84~Each investigation subject may be associated with exposure contacts, including unambiguous links to contacts in other jurisdictions.
4~Contacts of exposed entities may be traced, investigated, and monitored.
46~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to create new contacts from existing case records, and should also identify the contact type.
2747506~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must support contact exposure tracing by allowing one contact to be linked to multiple cases, and allowing multiple contacts to be linked to a single case.
2004~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to produce contact work lists for each investigator to use, and should allow sorting by priority or geography.
6~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should allow for analytical searches based upon multiple criteria.
30924684~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to produce charts, maps, and graphs that illustrate OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT data, such as epidemiological curves and the effect of vaccination or prophylaxis on the number of new cases or maps that illustrate the number of cases by zip code.
1065060~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should generate electronic data dictionaries for dynamic data, line lists, activity logs, aggregate data, and call back lists to assist the emergency response group and investigators in responding to and containing a health event.
11151~Reports generated by systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should clearly indicate the number of cases, the number of contacts per case, the number of cases with no known epidemiological link at the time of diagnosis, the laboratory results, and the number of vaccinations and or or treatments administered.
5942~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to produce pre formatted queries and reports to allow faster and more accurate reporting, while still allowing the flexibility of ad hoc reporting.
44~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to produce individual reports for each emergency team member or investigator.
11~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to compare characteristics of exposed and non exposed persons.
8~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should have the ability to produce lists of action items.
1866~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must have the ability to print questionnaires for multiple uses, including taking to the field, use during phone interviews, etc.
10~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to aggregate data.
168~Examples of aggregated data to be supported are: number of cases, number of contacts per case, and number of vaccinations and or or treatments administered.
632~Health event data should be aggregated into a centralized data store designed specifically to support analysis of events over time.
4~Data should be accessible for use with commonly available analytical tools.
40960~SYSTEM INTEGRATION AND DATA EXCHANGE Systems integration requirements specific to systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT are included in the section below and describe the types of data that OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to send and receive.
16~This section is limited to describing the types of data exchange that OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must support not the requirements for transporting the data.
48~Bi directional, secure exchange of data with partner organizations supports public health investigations across all levels of public health.
66918~Message construction and parsing, and secure data transport requirements that span PHIN functional areas are separately defined and should be reviewed in "PHIN Preparedness Cross Functional Components Requirements", available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
1312~Contact information for key response partner organizations should be stored in a local instance of a public health directory for associating to a health event, as described in section 2.2.2 Health event Data of this document.
26~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to accept data from other partner systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT.
9~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to create and send messages for laboratory test requests.
3429~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to receive, parse and process messages for laboratory test request responses, in accordance with PHIN Laboratory Test Order Response Message Implementation Guide, available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
9~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to receive, parse and process messages for laboratory results.
1~Laboratory results should be linked to laboratory test requests, which are linked to subjects.
1288~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to exchange messages for laboratory results with systems supporting surveillance, early event detection, and other preparedness areas.
24132~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to exchange messages for confirmed, probable and suspect cases, and the other case classifications that are noted in the PHIN message implementation guide, with systems supporting surveillance, early event detection, and other preparedness areas.
2~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must exchange messages for investigations and for exposure contacts.
30~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to receive, parse and process messages for countermeasures that have been administered.
3~Countermeasures that have been administered must be linked to the entity that was administered the countermeasures.
52~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to create and send messages for countermeasure administration requests.
34~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be able to exchange aggregated data.
168~Examples of aggregated data to be supported are: number of cases, number of contacts per case, and number of vaccinations and or or treatments administered.
3840~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should be able to provide the aggregate data necessary for health event monitoring to systems that support response tracking, such as the number of suspect cases, number of persons under isolation or quarantine, and the number of patients receiving countermeasures.
200435096~Mapping interfaces and data dictionaries must be clearly defined and included in data exchanges to indicate and describe both standard and customized fields because systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT are configurable to meet the individual needs of each event and therefore collect data specific to each event.
4~Message components should be grouped by observation type by systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT.
240~Systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT should support multiple file formats for import and export, such as databases, spreadsheets, messages, and text files, among others
180~Data exchange should support analysis and information sharing of possible health events at all levels of public health.
704~It is recommended that standards be used across systems supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT however, it is required that vocabulary standards be used when exchanging data.
48~Vocabulary requirements that span PHIN functional areas should be reviewed in "PHIN Preparedness Cross Functional Components Requirements", available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
25160~Operational requirements, such as system backup policies and procedures, continuity of operations, system monitoring, and employee training ensure that public health partners can effectively support activities in OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT and other PHIN functional areas.
2~Operational requirements specific to OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT are defined below.
33~Operational requirements that span PHIN functional areas are separately defined and should be reviewed in "PHIN Preparedness Cross Functional Components Requirements", available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
24~Policies and procedures for communicating information to appropriate stakeholders should be clearly defined.
564~Polices regarding data synchronization should be defined to support multiple deployment options as discussed in section 2.1 System Architecture of this document.
4~Configuration management protocols and personnel should be identified to support multiple deployment options.
1040~Protocols and personnel should be identified to support the set up and configuration of laptops and other field devices used in OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT investigations.
556500~Processes and personnel should be identified to support agent specific deployment packages, including syndromic grouping libraries and vocabulary sub sets, which will be used to efficiently collect data specific to the particular health event being investigated.
9330~Policies and procedures should be in place for determining when follow up and isolation and quarantine monitoring should be done as a part of a focused countermeasure administration and response effort, rather than as a function of contact exposure tracing.
2876~Systems and data supporting OUTBREAK MANAGEMENT must be protected from sabotage, corruption and unauthorized access, and must be available subsequent to a catastrophic event.
129~Security and Availability requirements that span PHIN functional areas should be reviewed in "PHIN Preparedness Cross Functional Components Requirements", available at www.cdc.gov or phin.
3~Privacy requirements ensure that sensitive information is not accessibly to unauthorized uses.

10~The Disputes System must be accessible by both internal and external users.

88~The Disputes System must allow the users to select disputable transactions (based on the age of the transaction) from a user interface and initiate a dispute (ticket retrieval request or chargeback notification) on the selected transaction.
432~The Disputes System must provide the user the ability to initiate a single dispute case on multiple transactions that belong to a single merchant.
6~The Disputes System will provide the user the ability to create or initiate a ticket retrieval request.
4~As part of ticket retrieval creation process the system must prompt the user to enter all the required information to create the ticket retrieval request.
10~The ticket retrieval request is a document that is sent to merchant inquiring the validity of a transaction.
32~The Disputes System must allow the user to create three unique types of ticket retrieval requests.
48~The three types of ticket retrieval requests are (1) Request for original receipt (2) Request for a copy of the receipt or (3) Request for a portfolio.
3087~A portfolio consists of documentation that would provide proof of a purchase such as the documentation that is received from a car rental agency that is more than a sales receipt.
16~The Disputes System must prevent external users from requesting original receipts.
2~Requests for original receipts are restricted to internal users.
112037~The Disputes System must provide a confirmation to the user upon the creation of ticket retrieval request that contains the following information the dispute case number the type of retrieval requested (copy original or portfolio) and the date that the merchant response is due.
14~The Disputes System shall allow the user to create or initiate a chargeback request.
4~The system must prompt the user to enter the required information to initiate a chargeback request.
802~The chargeback request results in a printed chargeback notification that is sent to merchant indicating that their account will be charged back if no proof is provided that the disputed transaction is valid.
18~The Disputes System must provide a confirmation to the user upon the creation of a chargeback request.
248929~The confirmation must contain the following information the dispute case number the type of chargeback requested (pending or immediate) and the date that the merchant response is due.
4~The Disputes System shall prevent the creation of duplicate dispute requests 100% of the time.
6~The Disputes System shall accurately provide a list of possible reason codes for a given transaction.
15184~The list of possible reason codes must be derived based on the type of transaction and the industry that the merchant belongs to according to the business rules defined for the Disputes System.
48~The Disputes System must provide the ability to view existing dispute cases.
2~The Disputes System must provide Search functionality.
4~The search method must include the ability to search by (1) the dispute case number (2) the merchant account number (3) the cardmember account number and (4) the issuer number.
174720~In addition to the above criteria the search functionality must further allow the user to limit the results of the search by a date range the type of dispute (ticket retrieval request or chargeback notification) the case status (open closed or all) and the dispute reason code.
21~A list of all disputes cases that meet the entered search criteria must be provided to the user.
204~The list of cases must differentiate the type and or status of the case by color coding the line item in the list.
39~For example all open cases will be yellow and all closed cases will be gray.
46~The Disputes System shall provide the users the ability to view the history of all activities that have occurred on the dispute case.
380~The Dispute System shall provide the users with the ability to follow up on a dispute case via follow up actions.
70~The list of available follow up actions for a given dispute case must be filtered by the status of the case and the access level of the user.
262~The Disputes System shall record the name of the user and the date for any activity that creates or modifies the disputes case in the system.
481~A detailed history of the actions taken on the case including the date and the user that performed the action must be maintained for auditing purposes.
511~For any systematic (non user initiated) action that occurs on a case such as the disputes aging process a case activity will be generated.

36~When a simulated unmanned aerial vehicle is in flight the NVEC Simulator shall reduce the battery every second by SIMULATOR BATTERY DRAIN VOLTS.
64~When given a land command the NVEC Simulator shall immediately change the unmanned aerial vehicle's current altitude to the ground altitude.
284~While responding to a goto command the NVEC Simulator shall continue moving in steps towards the target coordinates until the target has been reached.
4984~When given a goto command the NVEC Simulator shall compute the next coordinate based upon the normal vector and altitude of the current position and the normal vector and altitude of the destination.
2400~The simulator shall move the unmanned aerial vehicle with infinite acceleration and use numerical methods to hone in on the next coordinate which will be SIMULATION STEP SIZE meters from the current position along the travel path.
3208~When given a takeoff command the NVEC Simulator shall move with infinite acceleration the unmanned aerial vehicle to the takeoff altitude corresponding to its current longitude and latitude.
36~When a simulated unmanned aerial vehicle is in flight the Internal Simulator shall reduce the battery every second by SIMULATOR BATTERY DRAIN VOLTS.
64~When given a land command the Internal Simulator shall immediately change the unmanned aerial vehicle's current altitude to the ground altitude.
284~While responding to a goto command the Internal Simulator shall continue moving in steps towards the target coordinates until the target has been reached.
32~When given a goto command the Internal Simulator shall compute the next coordinate based upon the angle of travel and the step size.
3208~When given a takeoff command the Internal Simulator shall move with infinite acceleration the unmanned aerial vehicle to the takeoff altitude corresponding to its current longitude and latitude.
2~The Internal Simulator shall approximate the state of the battery
16800~When given a landing command the Internal Simulator shall move the unmanned aerial vehicle from to the ground altitude corresponding to its current longitude and latitude.
2288~When given a goto command the Internal Simulator shall update the location of the unmanned aerial vehicle at increments of SIMULATION STEP SIZE meters moving it towards the target destination until the destination is reached.
948~When given a takeoff command the Internal Simulator shall move the unmanned aerial vehicle to the takeoff altitude corresponding to its current longitude and latitude.

312192~The Flight Pattern for synchronized landing shall direct each unmanned aerial vehicle to synchronize at the final waypoint of the preceding route ascend or descend to a unique altitude synchronize fly to the longitude and latitude of the home coordinates synchronize and then descend to the landing altitude.
184832~The Flight Pattern for synchronized takeoff shall direct each unmanned aerial vehicle to takeoff to a unique altitude synchronize with other unmanned aerial vehicles fly at the unique altitude to the longitude and latitude of the first waypoint of the subsequent route synchronize with other unmanned aerial vehicles descend or ascend to the target waypoint and synchronize with other unmanned aerial vehicles to complete the flight pattern.
